A different version is found in the last part of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Bamidbar Rabbah 4" href="/Bamidbar_Rabbah.4"><i>Num. rabba</i>4</a>.</i> It is written: <i>David returned to bless his house when Mikhal, Saul’s daughter, came towards him</i><sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 6:20" href="/II_Samuel.6.20"><i>2S.</i> 6:20</a>, where Michal criticizes David for dancing in the street..</i>, etc. Who is <i>one of the empty ones</i>? Abba bar Cahana said, the most empty one, that is the dancer<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ʼορχηστής, ου̅, ‘ο.</i>. She told him, today the honor of my father’s house became obvious. One said about the family of Saul that one never saw a heel or a thumb of them. That is what is written: <i>He came to the sheep fences along the road and there was a cave</i><sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 24:3" href="/I_Samuel.24.3"><i>1S.</i>24:3</a>.</i>. Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: That was a fence inside a fence<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">This explains the plural used in the verse and shows that Saul went to relieve himself in the cave guarded from the outside by a double fence. In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 62b" href="/Berakhot.62b">Babli, <i>Berakhot</i> 62b</a>, this is quoted as tannaitic text.</i>. <i>Saul came to spread his feet</i><sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 24:3" href="/I_Samuel.24.3"><i>1S.</i>24:3</a>.</i>. He saw him how he lifted a little and covered a little. [David] said, how could one touch such a righteous body. That is what he told him, <i>behold, what your eyes saw today which today gave me in your hand in the cave and I could have killed you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 24:10" href="/I_Samuel.24.10"><i>1S</i>. 24:10</a>.</i>, etc. Is it not written “I had mercy on you” but <i>it had mercy on you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 24:10" href="/I_Samuel.24.10"><i>1S</i>. 24:10</a>.</i>, your modesty had mercy on you. <i>David told Michal, before the Eternal Who chose me over your father</i><sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 6:21" href="/II_Samuel.6.21"><i>2S.</i> 6:21</a>.</i>, etc. <i>And I was still humbler than this and I was lowly in my eyes, and with the servant girls you mentioned, with them I shall be honored</i><sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 6:22" href="/II_Samuel.6.22"><i>2S.</i> 6:22</a>.</i>, for they are not servant girls but mothers. How was she punished? <i>Michal, Saul’s daughter, had no child until the day of her death</i><sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 6:23" href="/II_Samuel.6.23"><i>2S.</i> 6:23</a>, implying that she died in childbirth.</i>. But is it not written: <i>The sixth Yitre`am, of his wife Calf</i><sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 3:5" href="/II_Samuel.3.5"><i>2S.</i> 3:5</a>. Only Michal is called “David’s wife” (<a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 25:44" href="/I_Samuel.25.44"><i>1S</i>. 25:44</a>). The problem that Yitre`am was born in Hebron is not addressed; it is discussed in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 21a" href="/Sukkah.21a">Babli, 21a</a>.</i>. She mooed like a calf and died.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Two Cohanim were standing in the upper gate which leads from the courtyard of Israel to the courtyard of women with two trumpets in their hands. At the rooster’s call they blew straight, modulated, and straight<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">The standard way of blowing either metal trumpet or ram’s horn, an extended single tone, followed by a repetition of high and low sounds, followed again by an extended single tone; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Rosh Hashanah 3:5:2-6" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Rosh_Hashanah.3.5.2-6"><i>Roš Haššanah</i>3:5</a>.</i>. When they arrived at the tenth step they blew straight, modulated, and straight. When they arrived in the courtyard they blew straight, modulated, and straight. They continued blowing until they arrived at the gate which was the exit to the East<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">From where they then went to draw the water from the Siloam pool.</i>. When they arrived at the gate which was the exit to the East they turned their faces to the West and said, our forefathers who were at this place, <i>their backs to the Eternal’s Temple and their faces to the East,</i><i>prostrating themselves eastwards to the sun</i><sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 8:16" href="/Ezekiel.8.16"><i>Ez</i>. 8:16</a>.</i>, but we, to Yah are our eyes. Rebbi Jehudah says, they were repeating and saying, “we are to Yah; and to Yah are our eyes.<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">While unnecessary repetitions in public prayers are forbidden (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 5:3:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.5.3.3"><i>Berakhot</i>5:4, Note 128</a>), and for the Babli all unnecessary repetitions in prayer are forbidden also in private, this does not apply to the Divine Name where there is a biblical source (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 34:6" href="/Exodus.34.6"><i>Ex.</i>34:6</a>) or in the case here, where the repetition refers to two different sentences with two different subjects (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 53b" href="/Sukkah.53b">Babli 53b</a>).</i>”
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sheqalim</i>5:2, Note 47. Since all sources of the Mishnah here have “the rooster” with definite article, not fitting for a person, the quote is not quite appropriate and the source certainly is in <i>Sheqalim</i>.</i> Rav explained for the House of Rebbi Shila, “when <i>gever</i> called<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 1:8:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.1.8.1">Mishnah <i>Yoma</i>1:8</a>.</i>” as “when the herald proclaimed.” They said to him, “when the rooster called.” He said to them, did we not state “Ben Gever”? Could you say, “the son of the rooster”?
Rebbi Jeremiah asked, the tenth from above, the tenth from below<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">It is not clear in which direction the steps are counted. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 53b" href="/Sukkah.53b">Babli 53b</a>.</i>?
Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, it is not written “and they were prostrating themselves,” but <i>they are prostrating you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 8:16" href="/Ezekiel.8.16"><i>Ez</i>. 8:16</a>.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">,</sup><sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">A form looking ungrammatical (which most moderns classify as scribal error), here read as indicating induced contortion, where people lie down flat first with face to the East and then to the West.</i>, that they were bowing down to the sun and prostrating to the Temple. Rebbi Abba bar Cahana said, <i>for two evils did my people do</i><sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jeremiah 2:13" href="/Jeremiah.2.13"><i>Jer</i>. 2:13</a>.</i>. Did my people only commit two evils? Did He not forgive in thousands? Only that they were bowing down to the sun and prostrating to the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">As example how one can do two evils in one action, idolatry and also blasphemy by equating bowing to the Temple with bowing to the sun.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> There are no less than 21 fanfares<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">By blowing metal trumpets, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:1-10" href="/Numbers.10.1-10"><i>Num</i>. 10:1–10</a>.</i> in the Temple and one does not exceed 48. Every day there were 21 fanfares, three at the opening of the gates, nine at the daily morning sacrifice, nine for the daily evening sacrifice, and for <i>musaf</i> sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">On Sabbath and holidays, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:10" href="/Numbers.10.10"><i>Num</i>. 10:10</a>.</i> they added another nine. On Friday afternoon one adds another six, three to make people leave work and three to distinguish between holy and profane<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">At the time of the start of the Sabbath.</i>.<br>Friday afternoon during Tabernacles there were 48: three at the opening of the gates, three at the upper gate<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">As described in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.5.1">Mishnah 5</a>.</i>, three at the lower gate, three at the drawing of water, three on the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">At the moment of the water libation.</i>, nine at the daily morning sacrifice, and nine for the daily evening sacrifice, nine for <i>musaf</i> sacrifices, three to make people leave work, and three to distinguish between holy and profane.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated: No less than seven and no more than sixteen<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sukkah (Lieberman) 4" href="/Tosefta_Sukkah_(Lieberman).4">Tosephta 4</a>:10 in the name of R. Jehudah.</i>. This Tanna<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sukkah (Lieberman) 4" href="/Tosefta_Sukkah_(Lieberman).4">Tosephta 4</a>:10 in the name of R. Jehudah.</i> considers blowing straight, modulated, and straight as one unit; the other Tanna considers each single one of them as a unit. You find to say, three for each tribe; Rebbi Jehudah says, three for each standard<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:5-6" href="/Numbers.10.5-6"><i>Num</i>. 10:5–6</a> (<i>Sifry Num</i>. 73), that the trumpets blown by Cohanim in the Sanctuary also were used to give the signals for departure of the tribes in the desert. The tribes were organized into standards, three tribes for each standard. Since for R. Jehudah three blowings form a unit, the question arises whether there were three or nine sounds heard for each standard.</i>. But it was stated, and nine at the tenth step. That is another one<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 7, which does not mention the tenth step, contradicts <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.5.1">Mishnah 5</a>.</i>. He who has “three on top of the altar” does not have “at the tenth step;” he who has “at the tenth step” does not have “three on top of the altar”<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Since Mishnah 5 does not mention that the actual pouring of the water on the altar was accompanied by trumpet sounds, the total number of units is equal in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:5:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.5.1">Mishnaiot 5</a> and 7; that number can be taken as a trustworthy tradition. The only difference in traditions refers to the place where the additional sounds were produced. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 54a" href="/Sukkah.54a">Babli 54a</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ze`ira said, this implies that they only blew the trumpet at the water libation<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">But not on the tenth step.</i>. If you are saying, for the drawings, one should state, three for drawing water today, and three for drawing water for tomorrow<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">Parallel to the trumpet blowing on the occasion of the daily wine libation; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Tamid 7:3" href="/Mishnah_Tamid.7.3">Mishnah <i>Tamid</i> 7:3</a>.</i>. Are these it? Are there not others, nine for <i>musaf</i> on the Sabbath, nine for the <i>musaf</i> on a New Moon, and nine for the <i>musaf</i> of the New Year’s day holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">Since blowing at <i>musaf</i> was mentioned in the Mishnah, the question arises whether separate <i>musaf</i> offerings require separate trumpet blowings.</i>? But it must follow him who said, <i>they shall blow</i>, in the course of the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 10:8" href="/Numbers.10.8"><i>Num</i>. 10:8</a>. Since the ram’s horn on New Year’s Day may be blown by any one of Israel, it follows that the trumpet blowing on Sabbath, holiday, and new Moon mentioned in 10:10, since it may be done only by Cohanim, refers to <i>musaf</i>. Since the days are enumerated separately it follows that on a New Year’s Day which is a Sabbath (and automatically a day of New Moon), three sets of <i>musaf</i> require three separate blowings. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 54a" href="/Sukkah.54a">Babli 54a</a>.</i>. The rabbis of Caesarea in the name of Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa: Even following him who said <i>they shall blow</i>, in the course of the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices, they were adding modulated sounds<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">In the scribe’s text reading תרועות for תקועות. Since R. Jehudah considers any sequence of sounds preceded and followed by an extended single tone as a single unit, there may be many modulated sounds within one <i>musaf</i> unit. The corrector’s correction of the non-word תקועות to תקיעות makes little sense in the context.</i>, they were not adding straight tones.
Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, harp and lute are the same<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">Denied by the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Arakhin 13b" href="/Arakhin.13b">Babli, <i>Arakhin</i>13b</a>.</i>, extra strings<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">Greek νη̅μα.</i> make the difference between one and the other. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, why is it called נֶבֶל? Because it whitens many kinds of musical instruments<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">“Whiten” means making pale by embarrassment. The word נבל of unknown etymology is explained by metathesis as לבנ.</i>. Rebbi Ḥuna in the name of Rav Joseph: By untanned leather and an abundance of strings it whitens many kinds of musical instruments. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish says, <sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 150:4" href="/Psalms.150.4"><i>Ps.</i> 150:4</a>.</i>עוּגָב is a water organ<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ‘ύδραυλις.</i>. Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel stated, there was no water organ in Jerusalem because its sound overhangs the melody<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">It drowns out subtleties. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Arakhin 10b" href="/Arakhin.10b">Babli <i>Arakhin</i> 10b</a>.</i>.
The fife of the Temple was from Moses<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Arakhin 10b" href="/Arakhin.10b">Babli <i>Arakhin</i> 10b</a>.</i> and was made from reed. It broke and was repaired but its sound was not as sweet as originally. They undid and removed, and it returned to its prior state. The cymbal of the Temple was from Moses and was made from brass. It broke and was repaired but its sound was not clangorous as originally. They undid and removed, and it returned to its prior state. The mortar of the Temple was from Moses and was made from brass. It broke and was repaired but it did not compound as originally. They undid and removed, and and it returned to its prior state. These are two implements which broke in the first Temple and could not be mended. About these it says, <i>polished brass</i><sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 4:16" href="/II_Chronicles.4.16"><i>2Chr.</i> 4:16</a>.</i>; scrubbed brass. <i>And two brass vessels, beautiful gold colored, valued like gold</i><sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 8:27" href="/Ezra.8.27"><i>Ezra</i> 8:27</a>.</i>. Two Armoraim. One said, one of them valued like two of gold. But the other said, two [of them]<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">A Roman copper coin, Greek ʼασσάριον.</i> like two of gold.
It was stated: Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says, the Siloam was giving water like an <i>as</i><sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is from <i>Sheqalim</i>8:5, Note 67.</i>. They said, let us enlarge it to increase its flow. They enlarged it and its flow was diminished. They fenced it in again and it returned to its prior state.
The organ. Rav and Samuel. One said, it had ten holes and each one produced a hundred different sounds. But the other said, it had a hundred holes and each of them produced ten different sounds. According to both of them it produced a thousand different sounds.
<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is from <i>Sheqalim</i>8:5, Note 67.</i> Which of the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and of the New Moon has precedence? Rebbi Jeremiah wanted to say, between the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and of the New Month, the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the New Month have precedence. The strength of Rebbi Jeremiah is from the following: Between the song of the Sabbath and the song of the New Month, the song of the New Month has precedence. Rebbi Yose said, there is a difference there since Rebbi Ḥiyya said in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: To make a proclamation to make known that it is the start of a new month. How does one do it? One slaughters the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and says for them the song of the New Month. But here, between the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath and of the New Month, the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices of the Sabbath have precedence, under the category: what is more frequent than another precedes the other.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On the first holiday of Tabernacles there were thirteen bulls, and two rams, and one goat. There remained there fourteen sheep for eight watches<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">The families of Cohanim were divided into 24 “watches” enumerated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 24:7-18" href="/I_Chronicles.24.7-18"><i>1Chr</i>. 24:7–18</a>. As stated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:8:2-8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.8.2-8">Halakhah 8</a>, in principle each watch was serving for one week in the Temple, the succession being determined by the order fixed in <i>Chronicles</i>; after watch 24 a new cycle is started with watch 1. But on holidays, all watches are equal, since all their members are obligated to appear in the Temple with the rest of Israel. On the first day there were 16 animals other than sheep; if each animal was given to a separate watch, there remained 14 sheep for the remaining 8 watches.</i>.<br>On the first day, six were sacrificing two each, and the remaining, one each. On the second day, five were sacrificing two each, and the remaining, one each. On the third day, four were sacrificing two each, and the remaining, one each. On the fourth day, three were sacrificing two each, and the remaining, one each. On the fifth day, two were sacrificing two each, and the remaining, one each. On the sixth day, one was sacrificing two, and the remaining, one each<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">The number of bulls decreased by one every day (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:12-31" href="/Numbers.29.12-31"><i>Num</i>. 29:12–31</a>); therefore the number of watches available for the sheep increased by one every day, the number of watches getting two sheep decreased by one every day.</i>. On the seventh day, all were equal. On the eighth day they returned to the lottery as on holidays<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">The lottery, to determine which Cohen received which office in the service, as described in <i>Yoma</i> Chapter 2, open to all Cohanim irrespective of their watches.</i>. They said, he who sacrificed today may not sacrifice bulls the next day, but they were taking turns<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">There were 70 bulls in all during the week of Tabernacles. Therefore 22 watches had the occasion to work on 3 bulls each, but 2 watches received only two.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated: All watches in the Temple doubled and tripled with bulls, except for the two last ones who doubled but did not triple<sup class="footnote-marker">128,</sup><i class="footnote">There were 70 bulls in all during the week of Tabernacles. Therefore 22 watches had the occasion to work on 3 bulls each, but 2 watches received only two.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sukkah (Lieberman) 4:15" href="/Tosefta_Sukkah_(Lieberman).4.15">Tosephta 4:15</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 55b" href="/Sukkah.55b">Babli 55b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar asked, would one start with them on the next holiday? Rebbi Yose said, the Mishnah says this, “on the eighth day they returned to the lottery as on holidays.<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">Since on all other holidays, when there are only one or two bulls, the lottery is among individual Cohanim, not watches, it is clear that the remaining two watches are not given preferential treatment on the separate holiday following Tabernacles.</i>” It only is a problem following what was stated in the name of Rebbi Nathan: On the eighth day there was no lottery. In Rebbi Nathan’s opinion, would one start with them on the next holiday?
<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">This is copied in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Chagigah 1:6:2-3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Chagigah.1.6.2-3"><i>Ḥagigah</i>1:6</a> (76c 1. 23,ח).</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, it was stated so that the eighth day was a separate holiday, a separate lottery, a separate benediction, a separate sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sukkah (Lieberman) 4:17" href="/Tosefta_Sukkah_(Lieberman).4.17">Tosephta 4:17</a>.</i>. Holiday, as Rebbi Abbin said in the name of Rebbi Aḥa, for all of them is written <i>and on day</i>, but here is written <i>on day</i>, to teach you that it is a separate holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">In the list of sacrifices for days 2–7 of Tabernacles the first words always are <i>and on day</i>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:17" href="/Numbers.29.17"><i>Num</i>. 29:17</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:20" href="/Numbers.29.20">20</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:23" href="/Numbers.29.23">23</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:26" href="/Numbers.29.26">26</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:29" href="/Numbers.29.29">29</a>,<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:32" href="/Numbers.29.32">32</a>, but the listing for the eighth day starts <i>on the eighth day</i> without connective (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 29:35" href="/Numbers.29.35"><i>Num</i>. 29:35</a>).</i>. Lottery, Rebbi Yose said, the Mishnah says this, “on the eighth day they returned to the lottery as on holidays.” Benediction, Illa<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">He is R. La as noted in <i>Ḥagigah</i>.</i> said, time<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">“Who let us live, and supported us, and let us reach this time.”</i>. Sacrifice, <i>one bull and one ram</i><sup class="footnote-marker">135*</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num</i>. 29:36. These numbers are characteristic of the High Holidays.</i>.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On three occasions in a year were all watches equal in the parts<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">Greek αι‘ μοῑραι [του̅ θεου̅], the fat which is forbidden for human consumption, including the entire animals of elevation offerings. All Cohanim of all watches equally participate in the service on the altar.</i> of the holiday and in the distribution of the shew-bread<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">While the removal of the shew-bread from the table in the Sanctuary is reserved for the watch serving in the week preceding the Sabbath and the bringing of the new bread for the following week is reserved for the watch serving normally in the following week, the removed bread is distributed among all Cohanim present for the holiday.</i>; on Pentecost one says to him, here you have <i>maṣsah</i>, here you have leavened<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 1:10:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.1.10.1">Mishnah 1:10</a>.</i>. The watch whose time is fixed<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">Who serves in the regular sequence of watches as given in <i>Chr</i>. They perform the service and receive the remainders of all sacrifices not explicitly prescribed for the holiday. This means that if one of the public comes to the Temple, his obligatory elevation offering on the occasion of his pilgrimage and the family <i>ḥagigah</i> offering are serviced by all watches, but additional sacrifices vowed during the year and brought on the occasion of his pilgrimage are serviced only by the watch on regular service.</i> brings daily sacrifices, vows and voluntary gifts, and all sacrifices of the public, and sacrifices everything<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">Anything not explicitly connected to the holiday by biblical decree.</i>. If the holiday is next to the Sabbath either before or after<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">If Friday or Sunday are holidays, the Cohanim coming for the holiday are forced to be at the Temple on the Sabbath and participate in the distribution of the shew bread, but not in any service on that day.</i>, all watches were equal in the distribution of the shew-bread.<br>If one day fell between them<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">The holiday is Thursday or Monday. In this case only the Cohanim living in walking distance from Jerusalem would not have to be in Jerusalem for the Sabbath.</i>, the watch whose time is fixed takes ten loaves and the one remaining takes two<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">This really means that the watch whose office terminates on the Sabbath (the outgoing) takes 5 breads, the one whose service starts on the Sabbath (the incoming) takes 5, and the remaining 22 watches together take two.</i>. On all other days of the year the incoming one takes six<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">And therefore the outgoing also takes six.</i>; Rebbi Jehudah says that the incoming takes seven and the outgoing takes five. The incoming ones<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">The plural refers to the members of the watch; the singular in the preceding sentence refers to the watch as collective.</i> distribute in the North and the outgoing in the South. Bilgah<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">No. 15 in the list of <i>Chronicles</i>.</i> always distributes in the South; its ring was fixed and its window closed.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 18:8" href="/Deuteronomy.18.8"><i>Deut</i>. 18:8</a>. The verse stipulates that all priestly prebends have to be equally available to all priests but then permits interpriestly trade offs. This is interpreted to mean that on holidays all are equal but for the remainder of the year by general agreement (or, as stated later in the Halakhah, by institution of Samuel and David) all income of one week is reserved for the week’s watch. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 56a" href="/Sukkah.56a">Babli 56a</a>; <i>Sifry Deut</i>. 169.</i>, <i>equal portions they shall eat</i>. I could think also on the remaining days of the year it should be so, the verse says, <i>except what was sold by the fathers</i>, except what fathers sold for the sons; you on your week and I on my week.
On Pentecost one says to him, here you have <i>maṣsah</i>, here you have leavened.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 1:10:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.1.10.1">Mishnah 1:10</a>.</i> There are Tannaim who state, here you have leavened, [here you have <i>maṣsah</i>.]<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition, unnecessary since the question is which of the breads, the azyme shew-bread or the leavened two extra loaves of Pentecost (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 23:17" href="/Leviticus.23.17"><i>Lev.</i> 23:17</a>) are distributed first.</i> He who said, here you have <i>maṣsah</i>, because it is beloved; he who said, here you have leavened, because it is frequent<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Even though this text is repeated in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sukkah 5:8:2-8" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sukkah.5.8.2-8">Halakhah 5:8</a>, it seems that text should read that <i>maṣsah</i> is frequent, and therefore leavened bread better liked. In fact the two breads of Pentecost are the only leavened breads permitted in the Temple area during the entire year and it is a general principle that in the Temple service the more frequent must have precedence over the less frequent.</i>.
Rebbi Levi said, all watches were given in the South. Rebbi Yose said, the Mishnah says so, “if one day fell between them.<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">Since the remaining watches together get two loaves, they must stand together at one place. North of the altar is the preferred place since it is the place prescribed for the slaughter of most holy sacrifices. Since the remaining watches are not better than is the outgoing watch, their place is South of the altar.</i>” Rebbi Judah ben Titus in the name of Rebbi Aḥa, the verse supports this Tanna: <i>and now what do you have ready, give in my hands five breads or what is available</i><sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 21:4" href="/I_Samuel.21.4"><i>1S</i>. 21:4</a>.</i>. But was Aḥimelekh from the outgoing watch<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">In verse 7 it is noted that the bread given was the shew-bread (which is most holy and forbidden for all except pure Cohanim.) But in v. 4 David had asked for any bread, preferably profane. At the same time by emphasizing five breads he intimated that he was dangerously hungry, in danger of his life, and therefore even shew bread was permitted to him (as understood in <i>Luke</i> 6:4). The number 5 refers either to Aḥimelekh being High Priest and taking 5 of the 12 loaves (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Yoma 1:2:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Yoma.1.2.3">Yoma 1:2, Note 167</a>) or, since his name does not appear on any list of High Priests, he was head of the outgoing watch, having 5 loaves to distribute following R. Jehudah. The argument then is rejected since there is no support for the statement that Aḥimelekh belonged to the outgoing watch; it rather seems that he was the organizer of the service at the Tabernacle. (S. Abramson, <i>Sinai</i>63, 5768, 193–197.) {The medieval commentators of Samuel reject any reference to shew-breads and refer to bread accompanying thanksgiving sacrifices permitted to any pure person.}</i>?
“The incoming ones<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">The plural refers to the members of the watch; the singular in the preceding sentence refers to the watch as collective.</i> distribute in the North and the outgoing in the South.” Rebbi Ḥanania the son of Rebbi Hillel said, to honor the incoming ones. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, not for this reason but because we have stated: “All who enter the Temple Mount enter to the right, and turn, and leave to the left.<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Middot 2:2" href="/Mishnah_Middot.2.2">Mishnah <i>Middot</i>2:2</a>. One enters the priest’s courtyard from the East. If then one turns to the right one is on the North side of the altar. The incoming watch divide the bread at their place of entry. Correspondingly, the outgoing ones divide in the South; afterwards they may leave turning to the left, through the gate in the East.</i>”
<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Sukkah 56b" href="/Sukkah.56b">Babli 56b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sukkah (Lieberman) 4:28" href="/Tosefta_Sukkah_(Lieberman).4.28">Tosephta 4:28</a>.</i>“Bilgah<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">No. 15 in the list of <i>Chronicles</i>.</i> always distributes in the South. Because of Miriam from Bilgah who apostasied and went to marry a general<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">Greek στρατιώτης.</i> of the Greek government. She came and patted on the top of the altar and said to it, Λύκος<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">“Wolf”.</i>, you destroyed Israel’s property<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">Her objection was to the excessive cost of Israelite worship. (While in <i>Deut</i>. the worship is restricted to “the place which the Eternal will choose,” it never is said that there can only be one such place. However the cost of the service detailed in <i>Lev.</i> makes it clear that only one such place was there at any given time.)</i> and did not support them at the time of their distress. But some are saying that its time arrived to serve but it did not appear; so Yeshevav<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">The preceding watch in the list of <i>Chr</i>.</i> served in its stead in the High<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">The word “High” has to be deleted. It simply is stated that Yeshevav served for two consecutive weeks.</i> Priesthood.” Therefore Bilgah always is with the outgoing and Yeshevav withy the incoming. Should it not have been eliminated from its place? You cannot do this, as Rebbi Simon said in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: It is hard before the Omnipresent to eliminate the chain of descent from its place. Could they not be made twenty-three? You cannot do this, as it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 9:22" href="/I_Chronicles.9.22"><i>1Chr</i>. 9:22</a>.</i>, <i>these are the foundations of David and Samuel the Seer in their faithfulness</i>. In their professionalism. It was a great feat of professionalism that no watch was taking and repeating in inheritance fields before the other could take<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">It is prescribed in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:21" href="/Leviticus.27.21"><i>Lev.</i> 27:21</a> that real estate dedicated to the Temple by a person whose ancestor received this land in the original distribution under Joshua and which is not redeemed by the next Jubilee becomes property of the Cohanim. This is read to mean that it becomes property of the watch which regularly is on duty on the day of Atonement in the Jubilee year (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 25:9" href="/Leviticus.25.9"><i>Lev.</i> 25:9</a>). (Property bought, not inherited, <i>must</i> be redeemed, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 27:23-24" href="/Leviticus.27.23-24"><i>Lev.</i> 27:23–24</a>.) It now is asserted that no watch repeats serving on the Day of Atonement in a Jubilee year after less than 24 Jubilee periods (or 1200 years.) Since we have no details about the calendar rules of the First Temple period, at the end of which the rules of original distribution became moot, the statement can be neither verified nor falsified. (There is another, most unconvincing, interpretation of this passage by <i>Pene Moshe.</i>)</i>. Rebbi Abbahu said, I computed it that no watch was taking and repeating in inheritance fields before the other could take.
“Its ring was fixed.” Rebbi Abba in the name of Rebbi Jehudah: They made the rings wide on top and narrow at the bottom<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">In the parallels, <i>Ma`aser Šeni</i> 5:9 (Note 184), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:11:2-10" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.11.2-10"><i>Sotah</i>9:11</a>), the reading is: wide below and narrow on the top. The rings were used to immobilize the animals before slaughter. Bilgah’s ring was not usable for the purpose.</i>.
“And its window closed.” That they could not use it for their knives, as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Mishnah Middot 4:7" href="/Mishnah_Middot.4.7">Mishnah <i>Middot</i>4:7</a>. The window being closed meant that there was no hollow space in the wall. Just as with the rings, the Cohanim from Bilgah had to use spaces dedicated to other watches to store their knives.</i>: “this was called the place of the sharp knives since there they hid the knives.”
